  139. Just, yes... believe the hype people! Prior to these sponges, I actually used the elf flat top powder brush to put on my liquid foundation (that elf brush btw is an excellent product as well). However, the bad thing about brushes, it that it is somewhat of an ordeal to wash them, and then you have to wait for them to dry. I am quite lazy, so in all honesty, my brushes do not get cleaned often enough. So enter these cute sponges. Number one, they DO give you better control of liquid foundation, allowing you to avoid the streaking from brushes, but also allowing you to slowly layer your makeup. I work in medicine, so I primarily do very lightweight, barely there, natural and conservative makeup. This is PERFECT for that type of application. However, if you want super heavy coverage, you can achieve that as well by tapping on additional layers. With heavier coverage, it still manages to look airbrushed. But the most beautiful thing about this product, is that it is great for lazy people like me! Cleaning the sponge is ridiculously easy. After each use, I just squeeze on a little face or hand soap, get it sudsy and wring it out like a regular sponge. The cool thing is that it doesn't even have to dry completely when you use it next since it is meant to be used damp. It does dry more quickly than a brush, so that is also a plus. The plastic container can also act as a \\"drying station\\". Inside the container - there is a small plastic ledge with an opening in the center, when your sponge is wet, it expands to twice the size, so it doesn't fall through the hole, so it can have Airflow under and above the sponge to help it dry! I don't know if this was an intentional design, but I think it's beautiful. Being able to clean your foundation tool daily is so much more convenient and hygenic compared to a brush, and it is less wasteful than using disposable sponges. It is also much more convenient for travel as it takes up way less space than a foundation brush, and can alsodouble as a concealer brush. One thing I did want to mention, I too have had some mild staining on the sponge from liquid foundation. It is mild, and does not take away my love for this product.   399. Although as a makeup artist, I have been used to using some of the best products on the market, I am also a skeptic when it comes to shelling out high amounts of money to buy the latest thing that is causing a huge stir. I tend to sit back and wait before jumping on the band wagon for most things when it comes to beauty.<br /><br />One of the things I avoided was buying the Beauty Blender. I had makeup sponges, brushes, and many other methods of application down under my belt, so I did not feel that I needed to pay such a high price for such a small item.<br /><br />Finally, I had a chance to try out a set of two Beauty Blenders, and was surprised to find that if I had been told several things about them to begin with, I would have purchased one sooner.<br /><br />HOW TO USE A BEAUTY BLENDER<br /><br />-First of all, a Beauty Blender is not a conventional makeup sponge. When you put it in water, it swells up a lot bigger than it is when dry.<br /><br />-Once it is wet, you squeeze out the water and then make sure that the sponge is damp.<br /><br />-With the damp sponge, you carefully tap the side of the sponge that you want to use (broad for large spots and narrow for narrow areas) and you bounce the sponge off of your skin quickly and making sure that you cover a lot of area before reloading the sponge, you cover your face with makeup.<br /><br />-IT WILL OFTEN LOOK LIKE YOU ARE NOT APPLYING ENOUGH- resist the temptation to apply too much.<br /><br />-With the tip of the sponge, blend the areas around the nose and inner eye, etc, well but lightly.<br /><br />You can also use this for cream blush and cream eyeshadow if you like(using the tip), but remember, you have to wash the sponge in between or you will get muddy makeup.<br /><br />CLEANING<br /><br />They have a special cleanser you can buy that is made for the sponge, but I use Dr Bronner's Castile soap diluted down or non sodium lauryl sulfate cleansers that are gentle (Avalon hand soap is one example) so that it won't deteriorate the sponge.<br /><br />PROS<br /><br />Easy to use, lasts a long time<br />Gives airbrush finish<br />Makes cream makeup products not dry out as quickly<br /><br />CONS<br /><br />Pink color will wash out for a while and look scary, but it is fine<br />EXPENSIVE<br />Can stain with some products<br /><br />WHAT THIS IS NOT GOOD FOR<br /><br />This sponge is not particularly suitable for<br />Powder products<br />Blush that is not cream<br />Lip products<br />Skin Cream<br /><br />FINAL COMMENTS<br /><br />All in all the Beauty Blender is one of the most important tools that I have in my kit for cream foundations and blush. I use it for doing foundation on men as well as women, and when using the right products, they are virtually undetectable when using the Beauty Blender as the application tool. When using brushes or conventional cosmetic sponges, the results took more effort. It is worth the money if you use these on a regular basis or if you have special occasions you want to look just right for.that it won't deteriorate the sponge.<br /><br />PROS<br /><br />Easy to use, lasts a long time<br />Gives airbrush finish<br />Makes cream makeup products not dry out as quickly<br /><br />CONS<br /><br />Pink color will wash out for a while and look scary, but it is fine<br />EXPENSIVE<br />Can stain with some products<br /><br />WHAT THIS IS NOT GOOD FOR<br /><br />This sponge is not particularly suitable for<br />Powder products<br />Blush that is not cream<br />Lip products<br />Skin Cream<br /><br />FINAL COMMENTS<br /><br />All in all the Beauty Blender is one of the most important tools that I have in my kit for cream foundations and blush.   654. I adore how this blends liquid foundation into the skin. It makes the skin look super natural and dewy afterwards. With a regular brush, you'd have to swirl it and really work it into the skin in order to avoid that sort of paintbrush stroke effect. With the beautyblender, you blot and stipple the foundation into the skin so that the makeup is perfectly blended in, and it is about a thousand times easier and faster to use than an actual stippling brush. It gives a flawless, dewy finish, and again, it is super fast and easy.<br /><br />Usage:<br /><br />Washing - Soak it completely through with water. I actually like to wash it before I use it, instead of right afterwards. Somehow, I think it's easier to rinse out the foundation that way. While it's completely expanded and saturated with water (don't squeeze out any water at this point), I pour some diluted Dr. Bronner's* liquid soap over the foundation stains on the sponge. Then, rub the soap gently into the stains to work it into a lather without squeezing out the water. You can rub out the stains more firmly as there are more bubbles. Run it under the tap to rinse out the last of the foundation and the bubbles. Squeeze out as much water as you can with your hands and then get the last of the excess moisture out by squeezing it while having a small towel wrapped around it. I found that washing the sponge like this tends to prolong the longevity of the sponge. If you're scrubbing at it while it's not lathered up, you have to scrub much harder, risking ripping the soft sponge.<br /><br />*[[ASIN:B0006NH946 Dr. Bronner's Magic Soaps Pure-Castile Soap, 18-in-1 Hemp Tea Tree, 32-Ounce]] I use Dr. Bronner's tea tree oil liquid soap. You can get it pretty much anywhere now - Target, Rite Aid, CVS, etc. I was already using it to clean my make-up brushes - it's excellent for that purpose. You only need a few drops for each brush, swirl it around your wet palm, and watch it lather up like crazy and wash away everything untilyour brush is like new. Anyway, I use it on the sponge for pretty much the same reason I use it on my brushes. It doesn't dry out the brushes or sponges, it works super well, you only need a little bit, and it's cheaper than buying little expensive bottles of brush cleansers. Plus, tea tree oil has some natural anti-bacterial properties, which is the main reason I buy it in this flavor instead of the nicer smelling lavender or citrus one (though it's no big deal if you use another flavor instead). Anyway, I discovered completely by accident when I was trying to use up the last of my first bottle of Dr. Bronner's that it works even better when you dilute the crap out of it with water. It's easier to work the sponge into a lather, and now that I know this, one bottle will probably last me two years even though I wash the sponge every time I use it.<br /><br />Application - The sponge should now be slightly damp with no excess moisture. Then, dot liquid foundation all over your face instead of directly onto the sponge so that the sponge doesn't accidentally suck up the foundation. Use the beautyblender to dab at, stipple, and bounce that foundation all over your face until the foundation is evenly spread and absorbed. Don't swipe or rub. Well, you could, but the finishing effect won't be as nice or flawless. The pointy end is best utilized on and around your nose and eyes. This is especially useful when you're applying concealer to the under-eye area or any blemishes around the face since you can control exactly where it goes. The round end is for everything else.<br /><br />And....that's it! It's super fast and easy to use (I cannot stress this enough), and it has such a great and natural effect on your skin. My mom saw me using it one day so I gave her my extra one, and she absolutely loves it. She's sometimes a little heavy-handed with her liquid foundation as a result of using just her fingers to work in the makeup. Using this, her foundation is blended in much more naturally and even the color looks better. She said that even her friends noticed a difference with how much better her foundation looks.
